 Serif&gt;&#13;Wholly-owned subsidiary through October 10, 2017, the date of BRAC&amp;#8217;s IPO, after which it was consolidated as a variable&#13;interest entity through August 9, 2019, the date of BRAC&amp;#8217;s business combination. BRAC was renamed Allied Esports&#13;Entertainment, Inc. (&amp;#8216;AESE&amp;#8221;) on the date of its business combination and all references to the surviving entity&#13;following the business combination are hereafter referred to as such.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company had determined that AESE, following&#13;its IPO, was a variable interest entity (&amp;#8220;VIE&amp;#8221;) and that the Company was the primary beneficiary of the VIE. The Company&#13;determined that, due to the redemption feature associated with the IPO shares, that the IPO shareholders were indirectly protected&#13;from the operating expenses of BRAC and it had the power to direct the activities of BRAC through the date BRAC afforded the stockholders&#13;the opportunity to vote to approve the proposed business combination. Therefore, BRAC&amp;#8217;s operations are included in the BROG&amp;#8217;s&#13;consolidated financial statements herein through August 9 2019. BRAC&amp;#8217;s IPO shareholders are reflected in our Consolidated&#13;Financial Statements as a non-controlling interest through BRAC&amp;#8217;s business combination on August 9, 2019. Under guidance&#13;in ASC 810-10-05-8 (&amp;#8220;Consolidation of VIEs&amp;#8221;) the Company&amp;#8217;s management has determined that BRAC, following its&#13;merger, should no longer be consolidated for financial statement purposes as the Company no longer had the power to direct the&#13;activities of BRAC. Following BRAC&amp;#8217;s business combination, the Company&amp;#8217;s investment in AESE is accounted for using&#13;the cost method as AESE no longer was considered a VIE and the Company now owned 12.4% of the outstanding common stock of AESE.&#13;All significant inter-company transactions have been eliminated in the preparation of these financial statements.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0pt 0&gt;&lt;u&gt;Income Taxes&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company recognizes deferred tax assets&#13;and liabilities based on differences between the financial reporting and tax basis of assets and liabilities using the enacted&#13;tax rates and laws that are expected to be in effect when the differences are expected to be recovered. The Company provides a&#13;valuation allowance for deferred tax assets for which it does not consider realization of such assets to be more likely than not.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify; background-color: white&gt;&lt;u&gt;Stock-Based&#13;Compensation&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0&gt;&lt;u&gt;Uncertain Tax Positions&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;In accordance with ASC 740, &amp;#8220;Income&#13;Taxes&amp;#8221; (&amp;#8220;ASC 740&amp;#8221;), the Company recognizes the tax benefit from an uncertain tax position only if it is more&#13;likely than not that the tax position will be capable of withstanding examination by the taxing authorities based on the technical&#13;merits of the position. These standards prescribe a recognition threshold and measurement attribute for the financial statement&#13;recognition and measurement of a tax position taken or expected to be taken in a tax return. These standards also provide guidance&#13;on de-recognition, classification, interest and penalties, accounting in interim periods, disclosure, and transition.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;Various taxing authorities can periodically&#13;audit the Company&amp;#8217;s income tax returns. These audits include questions regarding the Company&amp;#8217;s tax filing positions,&#13;including the timing and amount of deductions and the allocation of income to various tax jurisdictions. In evaluating the exposures&#13;connected with these various tax filing positions, including state and local taxes, the Company records allowances for probable&#13;exposures. A number of years may elapse before a particular matter, for which an allowance has been established, is audited and&#13;fully resolved. The Company has not yet undergone an examination by any taxing authorities.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;u&gt;Recent Accounting Pronouncements&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify; background-color: white&gt;From time to time,&#13;new accounting pronouncements are issued by the Financial Accounting Standards Board (&amp;#34;FASB&amp;#34;) that are adopted by the&#13;Company as of the specified effective date. If not discussed, management believes that the impact of recently issued standards,&#13;which are not yet effective, will not have a material impact on the Company's financial statements upon adoption.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Note 3 &amp;#8211; Going Concern&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;As shown in the accompanying financial&#13;statements, as of December 31, 2019, the Company had a cash balance of $108,756 and negative working capital of $1,289,995 The&#13;Company has no revenue source presently. Based on projections of cash expenditures in the Company&amp;#8217;s current business plan,&#13;the cash on hand would be insufficient to fund the Company&amp;#8217;s general and administrative expenses over the next year.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company continues to pursue sources&#13;of additional capital through debt and financing transactions or arrangements, including joint venturing of projects, equity financing&#13;or other means. We may not be successful in identifying suitable funding transactions in a sufficient time period or at all, and&#13;we may not obtain the capital we require by other means. If we do not succeed in raising additional capital, our resources may&#13;not be sufficient to fund our business.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Note 4 &amp;#8211; BRAC&amp;#8217;s IPO, Consolidation&#13;of BRAC and Non-controlling Interest&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;i&gt;BRAC&amp;#8217;s IPO&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;The registration statement for the BRAC&amp;#8217;s&#13;IPO was declared effective on October 4, 2017. The registration statement was initially declared effective for 10,000,000 units&#13;(&amp;#8220;Units&amp;#8221; and, with respect to the common stock included in the Units being offered, the &amp;#8220;Public Shares&amp;#8221;),&#13;but the offering was increased to 12,000,000 Units pursuant to Rule 462(b) under the Securities Act of 1933, as amended. On October&#13;10, 2017, the Company consummated the Initial Public Offering of 12,000,000 units, generating gross proceeds of $120,000,000.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;Simultaneous with the closing of the IPO,&#13;BRAC sold 400,000 units (the &amp;#8220;Placement Units&amp;#8221;) at a price of $10.00 per Unit in a private placement to BROG, generating&#13;gross proceeds of $4,000,000. BROG&amp;#8217;s investment in BRAC&amp;#8217;s common stock is eliminated in consolidation prior to the&#13;BRAC&amp;#8217;s merger on August 9, 2019.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;Transaction costs relating to the IPO amounted&#13;to $2,882,226, consisting of $2,400,000 of underwriting fees and $482,226 of other costs.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;Following the closing of the IPO on October&#13;10, 2017, an amount of $120,600,000 ($10.05 per Unit) from the net proceeds of the sale of the Units in the IPO and the Placement&#13;Units was placed in a trust account (&amp;#8220;Trust Account&amp;#8221;) and invested in U.S. government securities, within the meaning&#13;set forth in Section 2(a)(16) of the Investment Company Act of 1940, as amended (the &amp;#8220;Investment Company Act&amp;#8221;), with&#13;a maturity of 180 days or less or in any open-ended investment company that holds itself out as a money market fund selected by&#13;BRAC meeting the conditions of paragraphs (d)(2), (d)(3) and (d)(4) of Rule 2a-7 of the Investment Company Act, as determined by&#13;BRAC, until the earlier of: (i) the consummation of a Business Combination or (ii) the distribution of the Trust Account, as described&#13;below.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;On October 18, 2017, in connection with&#13;the underwriters&amp;#8217; exercise of their over-allotment option in full, BRAC sold an additional 1,800,000 Units and sold an additional&#13;45,000 Placement Units to BROG at $10.00 per Unit, generating total proceeds of $18,450,000. Transaction costs for underwriting&#13;fees on the sale of the over-allotment units were $360,000. Following the closing, an additional $18,090,000 of the net proceeds&#13;($10.05 per Unit) was placed in the Trust Account, bringing the total aggregate proceeds held in the Trust Account to $138,690,000&#13;($10.05 per Unit). BROG&amp;#8217;s investment in BRAC&amp;#8217;s common stock is eliminated in consolidation prior to the BRAC&amp;#8217;s&#13;merger on August 9, 2019.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;Upon the closing of the IPO, $10.05 per&#13;Unit sold in the IPO, including some of the proceeds of the Private Placements was deposited in a trust account (&amp;#8220;Trust Account&amp;#8221;)&#13;to be held until the earlier of (i) the consummation of its initial Business Combination or (ii) BRAC&amp;#8217;s failure to consummate&#13;a Business Combination within 21 months from the consummation of the IPO (the &amp;#8220;Combination Period&amp;#8221;).&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0&gt;&lt;i&gt;The Extension Meeting&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0 0pt 0.15pt&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0 0pt 0.15pt; text-align: justify&gt;On July 9, 2019, BRAC held a&#13;special meeting of its stockholders (the &amp;#8220;Meeting&amp;#8221;). At the Meeting, BRAC&amp;#8217;s stockholders considered a proposal&#13;to adopt and approve an amendment to BRAC&amp;#8217;s amended and restated certificate of incorporation (the &amp;#8220;Charter&amp;#8221;)&#13;to extend the date that BRAC had to consummate a business combination (the &amp;#8220;Extension&amp;#8221;) to August 10, 2019. The amendment&#13;was approved by the stockholders and filed with the Secretary of State of the State of Delaware on July 9, 2019.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0 0pt 0.15pt; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0 0pt 0.15pt; text-align: justify&gt;In connection with this vote,&#13;the holders of 9,246,727 shares of BRAC&amp;#8217;s common stock properly exercised their right to convert their shares into cash at&#13;a conversion price of approximately $10.29 per share resulting in $95,125,574 in Trust Account assets being distributed back to&#13;shareholders. In connection with the Extension, BROG loaned $30,000 to BRAC to be placed in the Trust Account for the benefit of&#13;the public shares that were not converted. The loan was non-interest bearing and evidenced by a promissory note issued by BRAC&#13;on the same date. The loan was repaid on August 12, 2019.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0&gt;&lt;i&gt;Business Combination Agreement&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;On December 19, 2018, BRAC entered into&#13;the Business Combination Agreement with Merger Sub, Allied Esports, Ourgame, Noble and Primo. The Business Combination Agreement&#13;was amended on August 5, 2019 and the Business Combination Agreement as amended is referred to as the Amended Business Combination&#13;Agreement. The merger closed on August 9, 2019 (the &amp;#8220;Closing Date&amp;#8221;).&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;Subject to the Amended Business Combination&#13;Agreement, (i) Noble merged with and into Allied Esports (the &amp;#8220;Redomestication Merger&amp;#8221;) with Allied Esports being the&#13;surviving entity in such merger and (ii) immediately after the Redomestication Merger, Merger Sub merged with into Allied Esports&#13;with Allied Esports being the surviving entity of such merger (the &amp;#8220;Transaction Merger&amp;#8221; and together with the Redomestication&#13;Merger, the &amp;#8220;Mergers&amp;#8221;).&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Mergers resulted in BRAC acquiring&#13;two of Ourgame&amp;#8217;s global esports and entertainment assets, Allied Esports and WPT. Allied Esports is a premier esports entertainment&#13;company with a global network of dedicated esports properties and content production facilities. WPT is the creator of the World&#13;Poker Tour&amp;#174; (WPT&amp;#174;) &amp;#8211; the premier name in internationally televised gaming and entertainment with brand presence in&#13;land-based tournaments, television, online and mobile. The transactions strategically combined the globally recognized Allied Esports&#13;brand with the three-pronged business model of the iconic World Poker Tour, featuring in-person experiences, multiplatform content&#13;and interactive services, to leverage the high-growth opportunities in the global esports industry.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Business Combination Agreement, which&#13;originally called for a debt repayment to Ourgame of $35,000,000 was amended to call for BRAC to (i) assume $10,000,000 of the debt&#13;obligations of Ourgame and Noble (including an additional $1,200,000 of accrued interest) and (ii) repay Ourgame the remaining&#13;balance of $23,800,000 by paying $3,500,000 in cash to Ourgame and its designees, issuing to Ourgame and its designees 2,928,679&#13;shares of BRAC&amp;#8217;s common stock and Ourgame retaining $1,000,000 of the proceeds of such loans to pay its transaction expenses&#13;incurred in the Merger. In connection with entering into the Amendment, BROG, as BRAC&amp;#8217;s founder, agreed to transfer an aggregate&#13;of 600,000 shares of BRAC&amp;#8217;s common stock held by it to Ourgame.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;Additionally, In July and August 2019,&#13;BRAC and BROG entered into several share purchase agreements (the &amp;#8220;Purchase Agreements&amp;#8221;) with several parties (collectively&#13;referred to as the &amp;#8220;Purchasers&amp;#8221;). Pursuant to the Purchase Agreements, the Purchasers agreed to purchase an aggregate&#13;of $18,000,000 of shares of BRAC&amp;#8217;s common stock in open market or privately negotiated transactions. If the Purchasers were&#13;unable to purchase the full $18,000,000 of shares of common stock in open market or privately negotiated transactions, BRAC will&#13;issue to the Purchasers newly issued shares at the Closing at a per-share price equal to the per-share amount held in BRAC&amp;#8217;s&#13;trust account ($10.30 per share), and having an aggregate value equal to the difference between $18,000,000 and the dollar amount&#13;of shares purchased by them in the open market or in privately negotiated transactions. At the Closing, BRAC agreed to issue to&#13;the Purchasers 1.5 shares of common stock for every 10 shares purchased by them under the Purchase Agreements. Additionally, BROG&#13;agreed to transfer an aggregate of 720,000 shares held by it of BRAC common stock to the Purchasers. Pursuant to the Purchase Agreements,&#13;BRAC is required to file a registration statement with the SEC as promptly as practicable following the closing of the merger to&#13;register the resale of any securities purchased by the Purchasers that are not already registered and cause such registration statement&#13;to become effective as soon as possible. The Purchasers included a $3&amp;#160;million investment from Lyle Berman, a member of the&#13;board of directors of both BRAC and BROG and the largest shareholder of BROG. Additionally, $5&amp;#160;million will be held in an&#13;escrow account and its usage will be limited to specific capital projects.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;Consummation of the transactions contemplated&#13;by the Amended Business Combination Agreement was subject to certain closing conditions including, among others, (i) approval by&#13;the stockholders of BRAC, and (ii) that BRAC have available cash in an amount not less than $22,000,000 after payment to stockholders&#13;who elect to redeem their shares of common stock in accordance with the provisions of BRAC&amp;#8217;s charter documents. This second&#13;condition was waived by Ourgame prior to the close.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;i&gt;Consolidation of BRAC and Non-controlling&#13;Interest&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company determined that BRAC, following&#13;its IPO, was a VIE and that the Company is the primary beneficiary of the VIE. The Company determined that, due to the redemption&#13;feature associated with the IPO shares, that the IPO shareholders are indirectly protected from the operating expenses of BRAC&#13;and BROG had the power to direct the activities of BRAC through the date at which BRAC affords the stockholders the opportunity&#13;to vote to approve a proposed business combination. Therefore, the consolidated financial statements contain the operations of&#13;the BRAC from its inception on May 9, 2017 through the date of the merger, when BRAC was determined to no longer be a VIE. BRAC&amp;#8217;s&#13;IPO shareholders are reflected in our Consolidated Financial Statements as a redeemable non-controlling interest prior to the merger.&#13;The non-controlling interest was recorded at fair value on October 10, 2017, with an addition on October 18, 2017 as a result of&#13;the underwriters&amp;#8217; exercise of their over-allotment option. During the period in which BRAC was consolidated, the net earnings&#13;attributable to the IPO shareholders are subtracted from the net gain (loss) for any period to arrive at the net loss attributable&#13;to the Company and the non-controlling interest on the balance sheet is adjusted to include the net earnings attributable to the&#13;IPO shareholders.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;i&gt;Deconsolidation of BRAC &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;Additionally, US GAAP (ASC 810-10-40) provides&#13;guidance on &amp;#8220;Derecognition&amp;#8221; of a previously consolidated entity or entities. Under this guidance, the Company shall&#13;account for the deconsolidation of a subsidiary or derecognition of a group of assets specified in ASC 810-10-40-3A by recognizing&#13;a gain or loss in net income attributable to the parent, measured as the difference between the combination of:&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;a) The fair value of:&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;table cellpadding=0 cellspacing=0 style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; width: 100%; margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt&gt;&lt;tr style=vertical-align: top&gt;&#13;&lt;td style=width: 0.75in&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td style=width: 0.25in&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: Symbol&gt;&amp;#183;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;any consideration received. In this case, the Company received no consideration.&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;table cellpadding=0 cellspacing=0 style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; width: 100%; margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt&gt;&lt;tr style=vertical-align: top&gt;&#13;&lt;td style=width: 0.75in&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td style=width: 0.25in&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: Symbol&gt;&amp;#183;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;any retained non-controlling investment in the former subsidiary or group of assets at the date the subsidiary is deconsolidated,&#13;or the group of assets is derecognized. In this case the fair value of the BRAC common stock at the close of the business combination&#13;was $11,950,475, and;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0 0pt 1in; text-indent: -0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0 0pt 1in; text-indent: -0.5in&gt;b) The carrying amount of the former&#13;subsidiaries assets and liabilities or the carrying amount of the group of assets.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;With the above guidance the Company determined&#13;that the effect of the deconsolidation of BRAC produced a gain of $20,448,687, which is a non-cash adjustment.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;As of December 31, 2019, and following&#13;the AESE merger on August 9, 2019, the Company owned 2,685,500 shares of AESE common stock. As a result, 537,100 shares of AESE&#13;common stock (the &amp;#8220;AESE Shares&amp;#8221;) are committed to employees and directors of the Company. Employees and directors are&#13;required to remain in their positions for a one-year period, with certain exceptions, to receive the granted shares. The AESE Shares&#13;had a fair market value of $1,396,460 on December 31, 2019. The Company recognized the full expense related to the Plan immediately&#13;upon the AESE merger date. Compensation expense of $2,309,095 was recognized upon merger and was adjusted on December 31, 2019&#13;to $1,396,460 due to changes in the AESE market price between the August 9, 2019 merger and December 31, 2019. Subsequent adjustments&#13;will be required each quarter to adjust the deferred compensation liability until the shares can be transferred to the employees.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;u&gt;Shares Transferred to Purchasers of&#13;BRAC Common Stock&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;As presented in Note 5, In July and August&#13;2019, BRAC and BROG entered into several share purchase agreements (the &amp;#8220;Purchase Agreements&amp;#8221;) with several parties&#13;(collectively referred to as the &amp;#8220;Purchasers&amp;#8221;). Pursuant to the Purchase Agreements, the Purchasers agreed to purchase&#13;an aggregate of $18,000,000 of shares of BRAC&amp;#8217;s common stock in open market or privately negotiated transactions. If the&#13;Purchasers were unable to purchase the full $18,000,000 of shares of common stock in open market or privately negotiated transactions,&#13;BRAC will issue to the Purchasers newly issued shares at the Closing at a per-share price equal to the per-share amount held in&#13;BRAC&amp;#8217;s trust account ($10.30 per share), and having an aggregate value equal to the difference between $18,000,000 and the&#13;dollar amount of shares purchased by them in the open market or in privately negotiated transactions. At the Closing, BRAC agreed&#13;to issue to the Purchasers 1.5 shares of common stock for every 10 shares purchased by them under the Purchase Agreements. Additionally,&#13;the Company agreed to transfer an aggregate of 720,000 shares held by it of BRAC common stock to the Purchasers. The Purchasers&#13;included a $3&amp;#160;million investment from Lyle Berman, a member of the board of directors of both BRAC and BROG and the largest&#13;shareholder of BROG. Mr. Berman received 43,800 bonus shares of BRAC common stock issued by BRAC and 120,000 shares of BRAC common&#13;stock transferred from the Company.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0&gt;&lt;u&gt;BRAC Convertible Loans&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Note 6 &amp;#8211; Fair Value of Financial&#13;Instruments&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;Under FASB ASC 820-10-5, fair value is&#13;defined as the price that would be received to sell an asset or paid to transfer a liability in an orderly transaction between&#13;market participants at the measurement date (an exit price). The standard outlines a valuation framework and creates a fair value&#13;hierarchy in order to increase the consistency and comparability of fair value measurements and the related disclosures. Under&#13;GAAP, certain assets and liabilities must be measured at fair value, and FASB ASC 820-10-50 details the disclosures that are required&#13;for items measured at fair value.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company has cash and cash equivalents&#13;and a revolving credit facility that must be measured under the fair value standard. The Company&amp;#8217;s financial assets and liabilities&#13;are measured using inputs from the three levels of the fair value hierarchy. The three levels are as follows:&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0 0pt 30.6pt; text-align: justify&gt;Level 1 - Inputs are unadjusted&#13;quoted prices in active markets for identical assets or liabilities that the Company has the ability to access at the measurement&#13;date.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0 0pt 30.6pt; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0 0pt 30.6pt; text-align: justify&gt;Level 2 - Inputs include quoted&#13;prices for similar assets and liabilities in active markets, quoted prices for identical or similar assets or liabilities in markets&#13;that are not active, inputs other than quoted prices that are observable for the asset or liability (e.g., interest rates, yield&#13;curves, etc.), and inputs that are derived principally from or corroborated by observable market data by correlation or other means&#13;(market corroborated inputs).&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0 0pt 30.6pt; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0 0pt 30.6pt; text-align: justify&gt;Level 3 - Unobservable inputs&#13;that reflect our assumptions about the assumptions that market participants would use in pricing the asset or liability.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0 0pt 30.6pt; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0 0pt 30.6pt; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;The following schedule summarizes the valuation&#13;of financial instruments at fair value on a recurring basis in the balances sheet as of December&amp;#160;31,&amp;#160;2019 and&amp;#160;2018:&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;table cellpadding=0 cellspacing=0 style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; border-collapse: collapse; width: 100%&gt;&#13;&lt;tr style=vertical-align: bottom&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td style=padding-bottom: 1pt&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td colspan=10 style=border-bottom: Black 1pt solid; text-align: center&gt;Fair Value Measurements at December 31, 2019&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td style=padding-bottom: 1pt&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;tr style=vertical-align: bottom&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td style=padding-bottom: 1pt&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td colspan=2 style=border-bottom: Black 1pt solid; text-align: center&gt;Level 1&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td style=padding-bottom: 1pt&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td style=padding-bottom: 1pt&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td colspan=2 style=border-bottom: Black 1pt solid; text-align: center&gt;Level 2&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td style=padding-bottom: 1pt&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td style=padding-bottom: 1pt&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td colspan=2 style=border-bottom: Black 1pt solid; text-align: center&gt;Level 3&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td style=padding-bottom: 1pt&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;tr style=vertical-align: bottom&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=font-weight: bold; text-indent: 32.75pt&gt;Assets&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td colspan=2 style=text-align: right&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td colspan=2 style=text-align: right&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td colspan=2 style=text-align: right&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;tr style=vertical-align: bottom; background-color: rgb(204

 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Note 9 &amp;#8211; Investment in Allied&#13;Esports Entertainment, Inc.&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;Following the close of BRAC&amp;#8217;s merger,&#13;the Company retained 2,685,500 shares of AESE common stock with a value, based on the closing stock of $4.45 on the merger, of&#13;$11,950,475. As noted above, in Note 5 - Related Party Transactions, 20% or 537,100, of the shares are committed to be released&#13;to employees one year from the date of the merger, or on August 19, 2020. Therefore, the Company recorded compensation expense&#13;and recorded a deferred compensation liability of $1,396,460 to recognize the commitment to employees.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Note 10 &amp;#8211; Stockholders&amp;#8217;&#13;Equity&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;u&gt;Reverse Stock Split&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;font style=color: black&gt;On February&#13;21, 2020, the Company effected a 1-for-300 &lt;/font&gt;reverse stock split (the &amp;#8220;Reverse Stock Split&amp;#8221;)&lt;font style=color: black&gt;.&#13;&lt;/font&gt;No fractional shares were issued. Instead, the Company issued the following to any stockholder who otherwise would have&#13;received a fractional share as a result of the Reverse Stock Split:&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;table cellspacing=0 cellpadding=0 style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; width: 100%&gt;&#13;&lt;tr style=vertical-align: top&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=width: 24px&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=width: 24px&gt;&lt;font style=font: 10pt Symbol&gt;&amp;#183;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: justify&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 10pt&gt;Stockholders owning 300 or more shares of Common Stock will receive (1) one share of Common Stock for every 300 shares owned and (2) cash in lieu of fractional shares upon the surrender of such stockholder&amp;#8217;s shares;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;tr style=vertical-align: top&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&lt;font style=font: 10pt Symbol&gt;&amp;#183;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: justify&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 10pt&gt;Stockholders owning between 25 and 300 shares of Common Stock will have their ownership of shares of Common Stock rounded up to one share; and&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;tr style=vertical-align: top&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&lt;font style=font: 10pt Symbol&gt;&amp;#183;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: justify&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 10pt&gt;Stockholders owning fewer than 25 shares of Common Stock will receive cash in lieu of fractional shares upon the surrender of such stockholders&amp;#8217; shares and will no longer own shares of Common Stock.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;/table&gt;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;Any cash payment in lieu of&#13;fractional shares were based on the volume weighted average of the closing sales prices of the Company&amp;#8217;s Common Stock&#13;on the OTCQB operated by OTC Markets Group Inc. (the &amp;#8220;OTCQB&amp;#8221;) during regular trading hours for the five&#13;consecutive trading days immediately preceding the Effective Date.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company was authorized to issue 500,000,000&#13;shares of common stock prior to the Reverse Stock Split, which remains unaffected. The Reverse Stock Split did not have any effect&#13;on the stated par value of the common stock, or the Company&amp;#8217;s authorized preferred stock. Unless otherwise stated, all share&#13;and per share information in this Annual Report on Form 10-K has been retroactively adjusted to reflect the Reverse Stock Split.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times

 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company has 20,000,000 authorized shares&#13;of $0.001 par value preferred stock. No shares have been issued to date.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times

 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company has 500,000,000 authorized&#13;shares of $0.001 par value common stock. As of December 31, 2019 and 2018, a total of 1,600,484 shares of common stock have been&#13;issued.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in&gt;&lt;b&gt;Note 14 &amp;#8211; Income&#13;Taxes&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;We account for income taxes under the provisions&#13;of ASC Topic 740, &lt;i&gt;Income taxes, &lt;/i&gt;which provides for an asset and liability approach for income taxes. Under this approach,&#13;deferred tax assets and liabilities are recognized based on anticipated future tax consequences, using currently enacted tax laws,&#13;attributable to temporary differences between the carrying amounts of assets and liabilities for financial reporting purposes and&#13;the amounts calculated for income tax purposes.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times

204)&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: left; padding-bottom: 2.5pt&gt;Deferred tax assets (liabilities)&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td style=padding-bottom: 2.5pt&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=border-bottom: Black 2.5pt double; text-align: left&gt;$&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td style=border-bottom: Black 2.5pt double; text-align: right&gt;&amp;#8211;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td style=padding-bottom: 2.5pt; text-align: left&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td style=padding-bottom: 2.5pt&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=border-bottom: Black 2.5pt double; text-align: left&gt;$&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td style=border-bottom: Black 2.5pt double; text-align: right&gt;&amp;#8211;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td style=padding-bottom: 2.5pt; text-align: left&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;/table&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;As of December&amp;#160;31,&amp;#160;2019, the&#13;Company has net operating loss carryover of approximately $26,764,183. Under existing Federal law, a portion of the net operating&#13;loss may be utilized to offset taxable income through the year ended December&amp;#160;31,&amp;#160;2037. A portion of the net operating&#13;loss carryover begins to expire in 2030. For tax years beginning after December 31, 2017, pursuant to the enactment of the Tax&#13;Cuts and Jobs Act (&amp;#8220;TCJA&amp;#8221;) net operating losses now carry forward indefinitely but are limited to offsetting 80% of&#13;taxable income in a tax year. Of the total net operating loss as of December 31, 2019, approximately $1,010,052 of the Company&amp;#8217;s&#13;NOL is subject to the TCJA net operating loss provisions.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;ASC Topic 740 provides that a valuation&#13;allowance is recognized if, based on the weight of available evidence, it is more likely than not that some portion or all of the&#13;deferred tax asset will not be realized. In 2019, BROG increased its valuation allowance from $9,735,771 to $6,010,207 to adjust&#13;for the decrease in net deferred tax assets primarily due to an unrealized gain recorded for book purposes related to the investment&#13;in Allied Esports Entertainment, Inc. The Company believes it is more likely than not that the benefit of these remaining assets&#13;will not be realized. The Company did not place a valuation allowance on deferred tax asset for BRAC related to the capitalized&#13;merger and acquisition costs.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in&gt;The Company files annual&#13;US Federal income tax returns and annual income tax returns for the state of Minnesota. We are not subject to income tax examinations&#13;by tax authorities for years before 2014 for all returns. Income taxing authorities have conducted no formal examinations of our&#13;past federal or state income tax returns and supporting records.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif; width: 100%&gt;&#13;&lt;tr style=vertical-align: top&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=width: 24px&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=width: 24px&gt;&lt;font style=font: 10pt Symbol&gt;&amp;#183;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: justify&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 10pt&gt;Stockholders owning 300 or more shares of Common Stock will receive (1) one share of Common Stock for every 300 shares owned and (2) cash in lieu of fractional shares upon the surrender of such stockholder&amp;#8217;s shares;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;/table&gt;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0 0pt 0.5in; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;table cellspacing=0 cellpadding=0 style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; width: 100%&gt;&#13;&lt;tr style=vertical-align: top&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=width: 24px&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=width: 24px&gt;&lt;font style=font: 10pt Symbol&gt;&amp;#183;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: justify&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 10pt&gt;Stockholders owning between 25 and 300 shares of Common Stock will have their ownership of shares of Common Stock rounded up to one share; and&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;/table&gt;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0 0pt 0.5in; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;table cellspacing=0 cellpadding=0 style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; width: 100%&gt;&#13;&lt;tr style=vertical-align: top&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=width: 24px&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=width: 24px&gt;&lt;font style=font: 10pt Symbol&gt;&amp;#183;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: justify&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 10pt&gt;Stockholders owning fewer than 25 shares of Common Stock will receive cash in lieu of fractional shares upon the surrender of such stockholders&amp;#8217; shares and will no longer own shares of Common Stock.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;/table&gt;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0 0pt 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;Any cash payment in lieu of fractional&#13;shares are based on the&amp;#160;volume weighted average of the closing sales prices of the Company&amp;#8217;s Common Stock on the OTCQB&#13;operated by OTC Markets Group Inc. during regular trading hours for the five consecutive trading days immediately preceding the&#13;Effective Date.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;On January 2, 2020, the Company deposited&#13;500,000 shares of its holdings of Allied Esports Entertainment Inc. (NASDAQ: AESE) pursuant to its brokerage account agreement&#13;with RBC Capital Markets, LLC. Under this standard brokerage agreement, the Company will be able to borrow funds secured by the&#13;value of the AESE shares pursuant to a standard margin account arrangement. The current value of the deposited AESE shares is $1,200,000&#13;based on a closing price of $2.40 as of March 5, 2020.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;On March 12, 2020, the Company entered&#13;into a business loan agreement with Cadence&amp;#160;Bank, N.A. (&amp;#8220;Cadence&amp;#8221;), as lender encompassing a $700,000 Promissory&#13;Note issued to&amp;#160;Cadence (the &amp;#8220;Note&amp;#8221;), a Security Agreement by the Company in favor of&amp;#160;Cadence and limited&#13;commercial guarantees by the Company&amp;#8217;s Chief Executive Officer and Interim Chief Financial Officer and members of the Company&amp;#8217;s&#13;Board of Directors (the &amp;#8220;Guarantors&amp;#8221;) (collectively, the &amp;#8220;Cadence Loan&amp;#8221;). The Note bears interest at a&#13;rate of 0.500 percentage points over the prime rate as published in the Wall Street Journal, currently 4.25% per annum, payable&#13;monthly, and is due on March 9, 2021. The Note may be repaid at any time without penalty. The Note is secured by all of the Company&amp;#8217;s&#13;rights, title and interests in and to 500,000 shares of the common stock of Allied Esports Entertainment Inc. (NASDAQ: AESE) currently&#13;owned by the Company and held in the Company&amp;#8217;s brokerage account with&amp;#160;RBC&amp;#160;Capital Markets, LLC.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;u&gt;Basic and Diluted Earnings (Loss) Per&#13;Share&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;Basic earnings (loss) per share (&amp;#8220;EPS&amp;#8221;)&#13;are computed by dividing net income (the numerator) by the weighted average number of common shares outstanding for the period&#13;(the denominator). Diluted EPS is computed by dividing net income by the weighted average number of common shares and potential&#13;common shares outstanding (if dilutive) during each period. Potential common shares include stock options, warrants and restricted&#13;stock. The number of potential common shares outstanding relating to stock options, warrants and restricted stock is computed using&#13;the treasury stock method.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times

Summary
of Significant Accounting Policies

Basis
of Accounting

the accrual method of accounting as generally accepted in the United States of America (U.S. GAAP) and the rules of the Securities
and Exchange Commission (SEC).




statements include the accounts of the following entities:



    
    
    
    
    

Black Ridge Oil and Gas
 Inc.
    
    
    
    

    
    
    
    
    



Wholly-owned subsidiary through October 10
 2017
 the date of BRAC&#8217;s IPO
 after which it was consolidated as a variable
interest entity through August 9
 2019
 the date of BRAC&#8217;s business combination. BRAC was renamed Allied Esports
Entertainment
 Inc. (&#8216;AESE&#8221;) on the date of its business combination and all references to the surviving entity
following the business combination are hereafter referred to as such.


 following
its IPO
 was a variable interest entity (&#8220;VIE&#8221;) and that the Company was the primary beneficiary of the VIE. The Company
determined that
 due to the redemption feature associated with the IPO shares
 that the IPO shareholders were indirectly protected
from the operating expenses of BRAC and it had the power to direct the activities of BRAC through the date BRAC afforded the stockholders
the opportunity to vote to approve the proposed business combination. Therefore
 BRAC&#8217;s operations are included in the BROG&#8217;s
consolidated financial statements herein through August 9 2019. BRAC&#8217;s IPO shareholders are reflected in our Consolidated
Financial Statements as a non-controlling interest through BRAC&#8217;s business combination on August 9
 2019. Under guidance
in ASC 810-10-05-8 (&#8220;Consolidation of VIEs&#8221;) the Company&#8217;s management has determined that BRAC
 following its
merger
 should no longer be consolidated for financial statement purposes as the Company no longer had the power to direct the
activities of BRAC. Following BRAC&#8217;s business combination
 the Company&#8217;s investment in AESE is accounted for using
the cost method as AESE no longer was considered a VIE and the Company now owned 12.4% of the outstanding common stock of AESE.
All significant inter-company transactions have been eliminated in the preparation of these financial statements.


 BROG
 and BRAC
 for
the period it was consolidated
 are collectively referred to herein as the &#8220;Company&#8221; or &#8220;Black Ridge&#8221;.
The Company&#8217;s headquarters is in Minneapolis
 Minnesota and substantially all of its operations are in the United States.



 the income
 expense
and cash flows from BRAC during the period they were consolidated have been classified as discontinued operations. For comparative
purposes amounts in the prior periods have been reclassified to conform to current year presentation. Additionally
 the assets
and liabilities from BRAC are shown on the balance sheet as assets and liabilities for discontinued operations.



interim reporting for an enterprise&#8217;s operating segments and related disclosures about its products
 services
 geographic
areas and major customers. An operating segment is defined as a component of an enterprise that engages in business activities
from which it may earn revenues and expenses
 and about which separate financial information is regularly evaluated by the chief
operating decision maker in deciding how to allocate resources. The Company operates as a single segment and will evaluate additional
segment disclosure requirements as it expands its operations.

Use
of Estimates

in conformity with generally accepted accounting principles requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the
reported amounts of assets and liabilities and disclosure of contingent assets and liabilities at the date of the financial statements
and the reported amount of revenues and expenses during the reporting period. Actual results could differ from those estimates.



of assets in the oil and gas industry. The oil and gas industry is subject
 by its nature
 to environmental hazards and clean-up
costs. At this time
 management knows of no substantial losses from environmental accidents or events which would have a material
effect on the Company.



which have maturities of three months or less. For the purpose of the statements of cash flows
 all highly liquid investments with

 which approximates market value. Cash equivalents on hand at December&#160;31

respectively.

and liabilities based on differences between the financial reporting and tax basis of assets and liabilities using the enacted
tax rates and laws that are expected to be in effect when the differences are expected to be recovered. The Company provides a
valuation allowance for deferred tax assets for which it does not consider realization of such assets to be more likely than not.


 2017 the U.S. Tax Cuts
and Jobs Act of 2017 (&#8220;Tax Reform&#8221;) was signed into law. As a result of Tax Reform
 the U.S. statutory rate was lowered
from 35% to 21% effective January 1
 2018
 among other changes. ASC Topic 740 requires companies to recognize the effect of tax
law changes in the period of enactment; therefore
 the Company was required to value its deferred tax assets and liabilities at
the new rate. The SEC issued Staff Accounting Bulletin No. 118 (&#8220;SAB 108&#8221;) to address the application of GAAP in situations
when a registrant does not have the necessary information available
 prepared or analyzed (including computations) in reasonable
detail to complete the accounting for certain effects of Tax Reform. The ultimate impact may differ from the provisional amount
possibly materially
 as a result of additional analysis
 changes in interpretations and assumptions the Company has made
 additional
regulatory guidance that may be issued and actions the Company may take as a result of Tax Reform.



 the Financial
Accounting Standards Board establishes a framework for measuring fair value in generally accepted accounting principles and expands
disclosures about fair value measurements. This Statement reaffirms that fair value is the relevant measurement attribute. The
adoption of this standard did not have a material effect on the Company&#8217;s financial statements as reflected herein. The carrying
amounts of cash
 accounts payable and accrued expenses reported on the balance sheets are estimated by management to approximate

required fair value measurement on a recurring basis.




cost and depreciated using the straight-line method over their estimated useful lives of three to seven years. Expenditures for
replacements
 renewals
 and betterments are capitalized. Maintenance and repairs are charged to operations as incurred. Long-lived
assets are evaluated for impairment to determine if current circumstances and market conditions indicate the carrying amount may
not be recoverable. The Company has not recognized any impairment losses on long-lived assets related to continuing operations.
Depreciation expense was $872 and $9
472 for the years ended December&#160;31
&#160;2019 and&#160;2018
 respectively.



came from management fees earned through its management services agreement with BRAC

as services are provided.

Basic and Diluted Earnings (Loss) Per
Share

are computed by dividing net income (the numerator) by the weighted average number of common shares outstanding for the period
(the denominator). Diluted EPS is computed by dividing net income by the weighted average number of common shares and potential
common shares outstanding (if dilutive) during each period. Potential common shares include stock options
 warrants and restricted
stock. The number of potential common shares outstanding relating to stock options
 warrants and restricted stock is computed using
the treasury stock method.


used to calculate basic EPS and diluted EPS for the years ended December&#160;31
&#160;2019 and 2018 are as follows:

had an anti-dilutive effect and were not included in the calculation of diluted net loss per common share. Stock options and warrants
excluded from the calculation of diluted EPS because their effect was anti-dilutive were 34

245 of December&#160;31
&#160;2019
and 2018
 respectively.

Stock-Based
Compensation

 all share-based
payments to employees
 including grants of employee stock options
 are to be recognized in the income statement based on their
fair values. Pro forma disclosure is no longer an alternative. Amortization of the fair values of stock options issued for services
and compensation totaled $100
526 and $310
731 for the years ended December&#160;31
&#160;2019 and&#160;2018
 respectively. The
fair values of stock options were determined using the Black-Scholes options pricing model and an effective term of 6 to 6.5 years
based on the weighted average of the vesting periods and the stated term of the option grants and the discount rate on 5 to 7 year
U.S. Treasury securities at the grant date and are being amortized over the related implied service term
 or vesting period.




 &#8220;Income
Taxes&#8221; (&#8220;ASC 740&#8221;)
 the Company recognizes the tax benefit from an uncertain tax position only if it is more
likely than not that the tax position will be capable of withstanding examination by the taxing authorities based on the technical
merits of the position. These standards prescribe a recognition threshold and measurement attribute for the financial statement
recognition and measurement of a tax position taken or expected to be taken in a tax return. These standards also provide guidance
on de-recognition
 classification
 interest and penalties
 accounting in interim periods
 disclosure
 and transition.


audit the Company&#8217;s income tax returns. These audits include questions regarding the Company&#8217;s tax filing positions
including the timing and amount of deductions and the allocation of income to various tax jurisdictions. In evaluating the exposures
connected with these various tax filing positions
 including state and local taxes
 the Company records allowances for probable
exposures. A number of years may elapse before a particular matter
 for which an allowance has been established
 is audited and
fully resolved. The Company has not yet undergone an examination by any taxing authorities.


position relies on the judgment of management to estimate the exposures associated with the Company&#8217;s various filing positions.



new accounting pronouncements are issued by the Financial Accounting Standards Board (&#34;FASB&#34;) that are adopted by the
Company as of the specified effective date. If not discussed
 management believes that the impact of recently issued standards
which are not yet effective
 will not have a material impact on the Company's financial statements upon adoption.


 the FASB issued ASU No. 2018-10

Improvements to Topic 842
 Leases
on certain aspects of the previously issued ASU No. 2016-02
 Leases (Topic 842) (&#8220;ASU 2016-02&#8221;) and have the same effective
and transition requirements as ASU 2016-02. Upon the effective date
 ASU 2018-10 will supersede the current lease guidance in ASC
Topic 840
 Leases. Under the new guidance
 lessees will be required to recognize for all leases
 with the exception of short-term
leases
 a lease liability
 which is a lessee&#8217;s obligation to make lease payments arising from a lease
 measured on a discounted
basis. Concurrently
 lessees will be required to recognize a right-of-use asset
 which is an asset that represents the lessee&#8217;s
right to use
 or control the use of
 a specified asset for the lease term. ASU 2018-10 is effective for private companies and emerging
growth public companies for interim and annual reporting periods beginning after December 15
 2019
 with early adoption permitted.
The guidance is required to be applied using a modified retrospective transition approach for leases existing at
 or entered into
after
 the beginning of the earliest comparative periods presented in the financial statements. The Company adopted this guidance
effective January 1
 2019
 and the standard did not have a material impact on the Company&#8217;s combined financial statements
and related disclosures.

 following
its IPO
 was a variable interest entity (&#8220;VIE&#8221;) and that the Company was the primary beneficiary of the VIE. The Company
determined that
 due to the redemption feature associated with the IPO shares
 that the IPO shareholders were indirectly protected
from the operating expenses of BRAC and it had the power to direct the activities of BRAC through the date BRAC afforded the stockholders
the opportunity to vote to approve the proposed business combination. Therefore
 BRAC&#8217;s operations are included in the BROG&#8217;s
consolidated financial statements herein through August 9 2019. BRAC&#8217;s IPO shareholders are reflected in our Consolidated
Financial Statements as a non-controlling interest through BRAC&#8217;s business combination on August 9
 2019. Under guidance
in ASC 810-10-05-8 (&#8220;Consolidation of VIEs&#8221;) the Company&#8217;s management has determined that BRAC
 following its
merger
 should no longer be consolidated for financial statement purposes as the Company no longer had the power to direct the
activities of BRAC. Following BRAC&#8217;s business combination
 the Company&#8217;s investment in AESE is accounted for using
the cost method as AESE no longer was considered a VIE and the Company now owned 12.4% of the outstanding common stock of AESE.
All significant inter-company transactions have been eliminated in the preparation of these financial statements.

 and BRAC
 for

interim reporting for an enterprise&#8217;s operating segments and related disclosures about its products

 2017 the U.S. Tax Cuts

possibly materially

Basic and Diluted Earnings (Loss) Per
Share

are computed by dividing net income (the numerator) by the weighted average number of common shares outstanding for the period
(the denominator). Diluted EPS is computed by dividing net income by the weighted average number of common shares and potential
common shares outstanding (if dilutive) during each period. Potential common shares include stock options
 warrants and restricted
stock. The number of potential common shares outstanding relating to stock options
 warrants and restricted stock is computed using
the treasury stock method.

Stock-Based

 all share-based

 are to be recognized in the income statement based on their

and compensation totaled $100

based on the weighted average of the vesting periods and the stated term of the option grants and the discount rate on 5 to 7 year
U.S. Treasury securities at the grant date and are being amortized over the related implied service term
 or vesting period.








 &#8220;Income
Taxes&#8221; (&#8220;ASC 740&#8221;)
 the Company recognizes the tax benefit from an uncertain tax position only if it is more
likely than not that the tax position will be capable of withstanding examination by the taxing authorities based on the technical
merits of the position. These standards prescribe a recognition threshold and measurement attribute for the financial statement
recognition and measurement of a tax position taken or expected to be taken in a tax return. These standards also provide guidance
on de-recognition
 classification
 interest and penalties
 accounting in interim periods
 disclosure
 and transition.


audit the Company&#8217;s income tax returns. These audits include questions regarding the Company&#8217;s tax filing positions
including the timing and amount of deductions and the allocation of income to various tax jurisdictions. In evaluating the exposures
connected with these various tax filing positions
 including state and local taxes
 the Company records allowances for probable
exposures. A number of years may elapse before a particular matter
 for which an allowance has been established

position relies on the judgment of management to estimate the exposures associated with the Company&#8217;s various filing positions.







new accounting pronouncements are issued by the Financial Accounting Standards Board (&#34;FASB&#34;) that are adopted by the
Company as of the specified effective date. If not discussed
 management believes that the impact of recently issued standards
which are not yet effective

 the FASB issued ASU No. 2018-10

Improvements to Topic 842
 Leases
on certain aspects of the previously issued ASU No. 2016-02
 Leases (Topic 842) (&#8220;ASU 2016-02&#8221;) and have the same effective
and transition requirements as ASU 2016-02. Upon the effective date
 ASU 2018-10 will supersede the current lease guidance in ASC
Topic 840
 Leases. Under the new guidance
 lessees will be required to recognize for all leases
 with the exception of short-term
leases
 a lease liability
 which is a lessee&#8217;s obligation to make lease payments arising from a lease
 measured on a discounted
basis. Concurrently
 lessees will be required to recognize a right-of-use asset
 which is an asset that represents the lessee&#8217;s
right to use
 or control the use of
 a specified asset for the lease term. ASU 2018-10 is effective for private companies and emerging
growth public companies for interim and annual reporting periods beginning after December 15
 2019
 with early adoption permitted.
The guidance is required to be applied using a modified retrospective transition approach for leases existing at
 or entered into
after
 the beginning of the earliest comparative periods presented in the financial statements. The Company adopted this guidance
effective January 1
 2019
 and the standard did not have a material impact on the Company&#8217;s combined financial statements
and related disclosures.

Entity's cash and cash equivalents accounting policy with respect to restricted balances.  Restrictions may include legally restricted deposits held as compensating balances against short-term borrowing arrangements

 a partnership interest or other means of exerting influence) in other entities
 for example consolidation or use of the equity or cost methods of accounting.  The accounting policy may also address the accounting treatment for intercompany accounts and transactions

Disclosure of accounting policy for computing basic and diluted earnings or loss per share for each class of common stock and participating security. Addresses all significant policy factors
 including any antidilutive items that have been excluded from the computation and takes into account stock dividends
 splits and reverse splits that occur after the balance sheet date of the latest reporting period but before the issuance of the financial statements.




























Disclosure of accounting policy for environmental remediation costs that are expensed during the period that resulted from improper or other than normal operation of a long-lived asset. This accounting policy may address (1) whether the obligation is measured on a discounted basis
 (2) the event
 situation
 or set of circumstances that generally triggers recognition of loss contingencies arising from the entity's environmental remediation-related obligations
 and (3) the timing of recognition of any recoveries. This accounting policy does not address: (1) accounting for pollution control costs of current operations or for costs of future site restoration or closure that are required upon the cessation of operations or sale of facilities (2) environmental remediation actions that are undertaken at the sole discretion of management and that are not induced by the threat
 by governments or other parties
 of litigation or of assertion of a claim or an assessment (3) recognition of liabilities of insurance companies for unpaid claims or (4) asset impairment issues.

two of Ourgame&#8217;s global esports and entertainment assets

Consolidation of BRAC and Non-controlling
Interest


 following
its IPO
 was a VIE and that the Company is the primary beneficiary of the VIE. The Company determined that
 due to the redemption
feature associated with the IPO shares
 that the IPO shareholders are indirectly protected from the operating expenses of BRAC
and BROG had the power to direct the activities of BRAC through the date at which BRAC affords the stockholders the opportunity
to vote to approve a proposed business combination. Therefore
 the consolidated financial statements contain the operations of
the BRAC from its inception on May 9
 2017 through the date of the merger
 when BRAC was determined to no longer be a VIE. BRAC&#8217;s
IPO shareholders are reflected in our Consolidated Financial Statements as a redeemable non-controlling interest prior to the merger.
The non-controlling interest was recorded at fair value on October 10
 2017
 with an addition on October 18
 2017 as a result of
the underwriters&#8217; exercise of their over-allotment option. During the period in which BRAC was consolidated
 the net earnings
attributable to the IPO shareholders are subtracted from the net gain (loss) for any period to arrive at the net loss attributable
to the Company and the non-controlling interest on the balance sheet is adjusted to include the net earnings attributable to the
IPO shareholders.




 US GAAP (ASC 810-10-40) provides
guidance on &#8220;Derecognition&#8221; of a previously consolidated entity or entities. Under this guidance
 the Company shall
account for the deconsolidation of a subsidiary or derecognition of a group of assets specified in ASC 810-10-40-3A by recognizing
a gain or loss in net income attributable to the parent
 measured as the difference between the combination of:




any consideration received. In this case
 the Company received no consideration.

any retained non-controlling investment in the former subsidiary or group of assets at the date the subsidiary is deconsolidated
or the group of assets is derecognized. In this case the fair value of the BRAC common stock at the close of the business combination
was $11
950
475
 and;


subsidiaries assets and liabilities or the carrying amount of the group of assets.


that the effect of the deconsolidation of BRAC produced a gain of $20
448
687
 which is a non-cash adjustment.





of $10
000 per month as part of an administrative services agreement
 which commenced October 5
 2017 and ended on the date of
the merger
 for general and administrative services including the cost of office space and personnel dedicated to AESE. BROG was
also reimbursed for any out-of-pocket expenses
 particularly travel
 incurred in connection with activities on AESE&#8217;s behalf
including but not limited to identifying potential target businesses and performing due diligence on suitable business combinations.
AESE paid a total of $72
903 to BROG for such services in 2019
 prior to the merger and while AESE remained a VIE and was consolidated.
The management services income of BROG and the management services expense of AESE as well as any balances due between the companies
for such services or reimbursements were eliminated in consolidation. Management fees earned by BROG of $466
595 subject to the
management services agreement between AESE and BROG in effect subsequent to the merger are not eliminated.
